		<title>What is the Secret of Chinese Economic Success?</title>
		<link>https://www.classcentral.com/report/review-china-economic-transformation/</link>
					<comments>https://www.classcentral.com/report/review-china-economic-transformation/#respond</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Alfredo Portinari Maranca]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Wed, 01 Mar 2023 18:12:48 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[Reviews]]></category>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>A review of China’s Economic Transformation Part 1: Economic Reform and Growth in China by The Hong Kong University of Science and Technology.</p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/review-china-economic-transformation/">What is the Secret of Chinese Economic Success?</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85478" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-main-banner.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-main-banner.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-main-banner-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-main-banner-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>This is an in-depth review of the free-to-audit course <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/econtransform1-8348">China’s Economic Transformation Part 1: Economic Reform and Growth in China</a> by <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/university/hkust">The Hong Kong University of Science and Technology</a> via Coursera.</p>
<h2>China economic transformation history</h2>
<p>In 1978, after nearly 30 years of socialist planning under Mao Zedong, China was one of the poorest countries in the World, with a highly inefficient and inward-looking economy.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85479" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-content.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-content.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-content-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-content-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>From 1978 through 2015, China grew at an average annual growth rate of 10% per year. Today, China has the largest GDP (Gross domestic product) of any country in the world and is the world&#8217;s largest trading nation. Deng Xiaoping undertook fundamental economic reforms that unleashed market forces, opened the country to the outside world, and lifted millions of Chinese out of poverty</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85480" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-instructor.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-instructor.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-instructor-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-instructor-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>All economists around the World try hard to think about what to do to bring economic success to emergent countries and are curious about how China could be the unique emergent country that indeed made it and became a thriving economy. China promises to wipe all the poverty, hunger, and underdevelopment out. How do they do it?</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85481" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-GDP.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-GDP.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-GDP-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-GDP-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>More than that, how can we grasp this knowledge without falling in the trap of political bias and preconception, with no cold war propaganda, analyzing objectively the most important aspects of the Chinese economy?</p>
<h2>The Instructor</h2>
<figure id="attachment_85482" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85482" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85482" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-presentation.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-presentation.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-presentation-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-presentation-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85482" class="wp-caption-text">Professor Albert Francis Park, course instructor.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The man for this job is Professor Albert Francis Park who teaches the Coursera MOOC <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/econtransform1-8348">China’s Economic Transformation</a>. You will learn the Deng Xiaoping principle of gradual reform, “crossing the river by feeling the stones”, allying millennial Taoist knowledge to modern economic technology.</p>
<p>Albert Francis Park came from Korea Development Institute, where he was a Research Assistant in 1988. After that, he passed a hard proficiency training in Chinese (1992) that enabled him to deeply study the Chinese reforms. Fluent in Chinese and English, Albert Francis Park Undergraduate as Bachelor of Arts at Oxford and got his PhD at Stanford in 1996. With academic positions at the University of Michigan, Oxford and Stanford, he is now an outstanding teaching professor at Hong Kong University and active in many institutes of emergent development and on the editorial board of the main journals of comparative economics and emergent development. He is the director of the Institute for Emerging Market Studies.</p>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85483" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-city.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-city.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-city-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Chinas-Economic-Transformation-Part-1_-Economic-Reform-and-Growth-city-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<h2>Conclusion and what’s next</h2>
<p>Chinese tradition involves hard work and this course is no different. There’s lots of information, reading, and material to study, so learn carefully, take notes, and study, because the tests are carefully made to check the assimilation of the didactic material.</p>
<p>After completing this course, as part 2 is still not available, I recommend the following courses: <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/chinesepolitics1-3790">Chinese Politics Part 1 – China and Political Science</a> and <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/chinesepolitics2-3791">Chinese Politics Part 2 – China and the World</a>.</p>
<figure id="attachment_85484" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85484" style="width: 1204px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85484" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Alfredo-Maranca-Certificate.png" alt="" width="1204" height="931" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Alfredo-Maranca-Certificate.png 1204w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Alfredo-Maranca-Certificate-300x232.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Alfredo-Maranca-Certificate-1024x792.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Alfredo-Maranca-Certificate-768x594.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1204px) 100vw, 1204px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85484" class="wp-caption-text">My certificate of completion.</figcaption></figure>

		<title>20 Most Cited Research Papers on MOOCs</title>
		<link>https://www.classcentral.com/report/most-cited-mooc-research/</link>
					<comments>https://www.classcentral.com/report/most-cited-mooc-research/#respond</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Heba Ledwon]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Wed, 01 Mar 2023 13:45:04 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[Analysis]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[MOOC Research]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://www.classcentral.com/report/?p=72261</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>To get an overview of the topics and trends in the research on MOOCs, Class Central has created a list of the most cited research papers on MOOCs.</p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/most-cited-mooc-research/">20 Most Cited Research Papers on MOOCs</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<figure id="attachment_72265" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-72265" style="width: 1920px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-72265" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/patrick-robert-doyle-OvXht_wi5Ew-unsplash.jpg" alt="" width="1920" height="1200" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/patrick-robert-doyle-OvXht_wi5Ew-unsplash.jpg 1920w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/patrick-robert-doyle-OvXht_wi5Ew-unsplash-300x188.jpg 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/patrick-robert-doyle-OvXht_wi5Ew-unsplash-1024x640.jpg 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/patrick-robert-doyle-OvXht_wi5Ew-unsplash-768x480.jpg 768w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/patrick-robert-doyle-OvXht_wi5Ew-unsplash-1536x960.jpg 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-72265" class="wp-caption-text">Photo by <a href="https://unsplash.com/@teapowered?utm_source=unsplash&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_content=creditCopyText">Patrick Robert Doyle</a> on <a href="https://unsplash.com/?utm_source=unsplash&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_content=creditCopyText">Unsplash</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The research on <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/help/moocs">Massive Open Online Courses</a> (MOOCs) is at least as old as the introduction of the first MOOC. MOOCs and learning analytics gave researchers a unique opportunity to follow students closely on their learning path. This generated new findings on the learning habits of students, developed the knowledge on learning technology further and derived evidence-based recommendations for instructional designers. To get an overview of the topics and trends in the research on MOOCs we have created a list of the most cited research papers on MOOCs.</p>
<h2>Methodology</h2>
<p>In an attempt to have an overview of the most cited research papers in the field of Massive Open Online Courses (MOOCs) on Google Scholar, we combined the search results of relevant search terms (and their plurals) “MOOC” (about 61K results), “Massive Open Online Course” (about 35K), and “e-learning” (about 630K) in the following list. We have only included articles published since 2008. The short description under the title is extracted from the abstracts of the articles.</p>
<h2>Twenty Most Cited MOOC Research Papers</h2>
<p><strong><a href="https://dl.acm.org/doi/abs/10.1145/2556325.2566239">How video production affects student engagement: An empirical study of MOOC videos</a></strong> (2014) by PJ Guo, J Kim, R Rubin<br />
The study analyzes 6.9 million video watching sessions across four courses on edX to measure student engagement with online educational videos. The findings suggest that shorter videos, informal talking-head videos, and Khan-style tablet drawings are more engaging. The study also highlights the importance of understanding how students engage with different types of videos and recommends that instructors and video producers leverage the online video format accordingly. The anonymized data set and analysis scripts are publicly available.</p>
<p><strong><a href="https://jime.open.ac.uk/articles/10.5334/2012-18">Making sense of MOOCs: Musings in a maze of myth, paradox and possibility</a></strong> (2012) by J Daniel<br />
This paper provides a history of MOOCs and contextualizes them within the evolution of educational technology and open/distance learning. While the hype around MOOCs focuses on their scale, the real revolution is that universities with scarcity at the heart of their business models are embracing openness. The paper explores paradoxes and debunks myths associated with the MOOC movement, highlighting the potential for competition among participating institutions to improve teaching quality and reduce costs of higher education.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.erudit.org/en/journals/irrodl/1900-v1-n1-irrodl05095/1066922ar/abstract/"><strong>MOOCs: A systematic study of the published literature 2008-2012</strong></a> (2013) Tharindu Rekha Liyanagunawardena, Andrew Alexandar Adams, and Shirley Ann Williams<br />
This paper presents a systematic review of published MOOC literature from 2008-2012, identifying 45 peer-reviewed papers across eight areas of interest. MOOCs are recognised as having the potential to deliver education globally, and this review provides a quantitative analysis of publications according to publication type, year of publication, and contributors. The authors explore future research directions guided by gaps in the literature.</p>
<p><strong><a href="https://eric.ed.gov/?id=ej1062850">Studying learning in the worldwide classroom research into edX&#8217;s first MOOC.</a> </strong>(2013) by Lori Breslow, David E. Pritchard, Jennifer DeBoer, Glenda S. Stump, Andrew D. Ho, Daniel T. Seaton<br />
&#8220;Circuits and Electronics&#8221; was the first MOOC developed by edX, attracting over 155,000 students in 2012. Researchers analyzed the data generated by the course and found insights about students&#8217; resource use and achievement. A second stage of research is underway to examine the background and capabilities of the students and their interactions with the course&#8217;s components to understand their level of success.</p>
<p><a href="https://dl.acm.org/doi/abs/10.1145/2460296.2460330"><strong>Deconstructing disengagement: analyzing learner subpopulations in massive open online courses</strong></a> (2013) by René F. Kizilcec, Chris Piech, Emily Schneider<br />
A classification method has been developed to identify longitudinal engagement trajectories in three computer science MOOCs. This method identifies four prototypical trajectories of engagement, including learners who stay engaged without taking assessments. The trajectories can be used to compare learner engagement across different courses and demographics, informing future interventions, research, and design directions for MOOCs.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.erudit.org/en/journals/irrodl/1900-v1-n1-irrodl04927/1065273ar/abstract/"><strong>Initial Trends in Enrolment and Completion of Massive Open Online Courses</strong></a> (2014) by K Jordan<br />
This paper examines the public data available on enrolment and completion rates in MOOCs. The average course enrolls 43,000 students, with a completion rate of 6.5%, and enrolment numbers are decreasing over time. Completion rates are consistent across time, university rank, and total enrolment, but negatively correlated with course length. The study provides a more accurate view of how the MOOC field is developing.</p>
<p><strong><a href="https://d1wqtxts1xzle7.cloudfront.net/43171365/MOOC_Final-libre.pdf?1456696115=&amp;response-content-disposition=inline%3B+filename%3DThe_MOOC_model_for_digital_practice.pdf&amp;Expires=1677538572&amp;Signature=Wn464URzFOVp72APrpml-1DVRfu5p0ytt7~yUS08yic4yFK73-fxywZUfR3rkbcCiBSeVrG0F2-rRhr4BktoIiNAwvjnPxQ4MoqlQtYNJ8hQUEl4j1ct-jDydKRKN3vZDIGrlbOSzPvvtyERO4~3amBCUSddLAF6~Ffkxmr39-YrrWIyfnnqyXUQUK9pu42YbH0cBIQFcERFvWFtgbmH8vtRLL0DE5ZV35MPl6UKH3jSd-ANRMy8x5bDnaF~oov4wJG7hRN1ve-cT3aW4dL1wpN3Fk2fc1~fvsSxgMdcXtrh6mMDSjeiDg2U4MZpwftkbUHjkyN0BZKheQXof4ta2Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAJLOHF5GGSLRBV4ZA">The MOOC model for digital practice</a> </strong>(2010) by A McAuley, B Stewart, G Siemens, D Cormier<br />
The report explores the relationship between Massive Online Open Courses (MOOCs) and the digital economy in Canada. It argues that a prosperous digital ecosystem requires a citizenry with the knowledge, skills, and attitudes necessary to participate in that economy. The report presents a Canadian model for how MOOCs can address this need and includes four digital videos to supplement the printed report.</p>
<p><strong><a href="https://www.erudit.org/en/journals/irrodl/1900-v1-n1-irrodl05132/1067613ar/abstract/">The Challenges to Connectivist Learning on Open Online Networks: Learning Experiences during a Massive Open Online Course</a></strong> (2011) by R Kop<br />
Self-directed learning on open online networks is now a possibility as communication and resources can be combined to create learning environments. But is it really? There are some challenges that might prevent learners from having a quality learning experience. This paper raises questions on levels of learner autonomy, presence, and critical literacies required in active connectivist learning.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S1747938X14000128"><strong>Students’ and instructors’ use of massive open online courses (MOOCs): Motivations and challenges</strong></a> (2014) by KF Hew, WS Cheung<br />
Summary of summary: The paper reviews published literature on MOOCs, identifying reasons for student enrollment as learning, curiosity, challenge, and certification, while high dropout rates result from insufficient incentives, poor comprehension, and other priorities. Instructors&#8217; motivations are intrigue, personal rewards, and altruism, but they face difficulties in evaluating student work, feedback, and low participation. MOOC education quality and assessment are unresolved issues.</p>
<p><strong><a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S000768131630009X">Higher education and the digital revolution: About MOOCs, SPOCs, social media, and the Cookie Monster</a></strong> (2016) by AM Kaplan, M Haenlein<br />
This article provides a nuanced analysis of online distance learning, including an overview of its historical evolution, key concepts, optimal target group, and corresponding frameworks for driving intrinsic student motivation and choosing a successful online teacher. The benefits of offering online distance learning are outlined, and the specific connection between online distance learning and social media is discussed, focusing on the difference between xMOOCs and cMOOCs.</p>
<p><a href="https://e-space.mmu.ac.uk/619735/"><strong>MOOCs and open education: Implications for higher education</strong></a> (2013) by Li Yuan and SJ Powell<br />
This report provides decision makers in higher education institutions with an understanding of MOOCs and trends towards greater openness in higher education, including the changes currently taking place in higher education due to globalization and constrained budgets. The report, written from a UK perspective, uses a literature review to identify current debates about new course provision, funding changes, and implications for greater openness in higher education. The theory of disruptive innovation is used to help institutions address policy and strategy questions.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S036013151400178X"><strong>Instructional quality of Massive Open Online Courses (MOOCs)</strong></a> (2015) by A Margaryan, M Bianco, A Littlejohn<br />
In this study, the instructional design quality of 76 randomly selected Massive Open Online Courses (MOOCs) was analyzed using a course survey instrument. Two types of MOOCs were analyzed and their instructional design quality was assessed and compared. The majority of MOOCs scored poorly on most instructional design principles, indicating that although most MOOCs are well-packaged, their instructional design quality is low. Implications for practice and ideas for future research are outlined.</p>
<p><strong><a href="https://eric.ed.gov/?id=ej982976">MOOCs and the AI-Stanford Like Courses: Two Successful and Distinct Course Formats for Massive Open Online Courses.</a> </strong>(2012) by CO Rodriguez<br />
This article discusses the rise of open online courses (OOCs) with a massive number of students, such as the artificial intelligence course CS221 offered by Stanford in 2011 which attracted 160,000 registered students. While both AI and connectivist MOOCs (c MOOCs) have been identified as equivalent in many instances, the article argues that the format associated with c-MOOCs is unique and different from AI due to its participative pedagogical model, which aligns with connectivist pedagogy. The article also discusses the evolution of distance education pedagogy, which has progressed from cognitive-behaviorist to social constructivist to connectivist models. The article includes tables and figures for further detail.</p>
<p><a href="https://dl.acm.org/doi/abs/10.1145/2460296.2460332"><strong>MOOCs and the funnel of participation</strong></a> (2013) by Doug Clow<br />
This article discusses how Massive Online Open Courses (MOOCs) present challenges for mainstream learning analytics practices, and highlights the high dropout rates in MOOCs compared to traditional education. The article introduces the metaphor of a &#8216;funnel of participation&#8217; to describe the pattern of steep drop-offs and unequal participation in MOOCs and similar learning environments. Empirical data from three online learning sites are presented to support the funnel of participation concept. The article concludes with a discussion on the implications of the funnel for MOOCs, formal education, and learning analytics practice.</p>
<p><a href="https://pure.port.ac.uk/ws/portalfiles/portal/108952/The_Ideals_and_Realilty_of_Participating_in_a_MOOC.pdf"><strong>The ideals and reality of participating in a MOOC</strong></a> (2010) by J Mackness, S Mak, R Williams<br />
The paper discusses a MOOC called ‘CCK08’ which focused on the emergent practices and theory of Connectivism. Over 2000 participants from around the world registered for the course, with some enrolled for credit. The paper explores the perspectives of participants on their learning experiences in the course in relation to the characteristics of connectivism outlined by Stephen Downes. The research found that the more autonomous, diverse and open the course, and the more connected the learners, the more potential for learning to be limited by the lack of structure, support, and moderation normally associated with an online course. The research suggests that further studies are needed to investigate whether a large open online network can be fused with a course.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0360131516301798"><strong>Self-regulated learning strategies predict learner behavior and goal attainment in Massive Open Online Courses</strong></a> (2017) by RF Kizilcec, M Pérez-Sanagustín, JJ Maldonado<br />
This paper discusses the importance of self-regulated learning (SRL) skills in Massive Open Online Courses (MOOCs) and how effective implementation of learner support systems requires an understanding of which SRL strategies are most effective and how these strategies manifest in online behavior. The authors investigated SRL in a sample of 4,831 learners across six MOOCs and found that goal setting and strategic planning predicted attainment of personal course goals, while help seeking was associated with lower goal attainment. Learners with stronger SRL skills were more likely to revisit previously studied course materials, especially course assessments. The paper concludes by discussing implications for theory and the development of learning environments that provide adaptive support.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.erudit.org/en/journals/irrodl/1900-v1-n1-irrodl05118/1067320ar/abstract/"><strong>A Pedagogy of Abundance or a Pedagogy to Support Human Beings? Participant Support on Massive Open Online Courses</strong></a> (2011) by Rita Kop, Hélène Fournier and John Sui Fai Mak<br />
This paper explores how new technologies could impact the design of learning environments, with a focus on the roles of educators and learners in creating networked learning experiences on MOOCs. The paper proposes a pedagogy that supports learners and course facilitators in creating resources and learning places through collaboration, building a community of learners, and utilizing information flows on networks. This aligns with the idea of emergent learning, where actors and systems co-evolve in a MOOC, and the level of presence of actors on the MOOC influences learning outcomes.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.irrodl.org/index.php/irrodl/article/view/643"><strong>The technological dimension of a massive open online course: The case of the CCK08 course tools</strong></a> (2009) A Fini<br />
This paper focuses on technological aspects of the Connectivism and Connective Knowledge (CCK08) MOOC and investigates attitudes of lifelong learners towards learning network technologies. Findings show that time constraints, language barriers, and ICT skills affected participants’ choice of tools, and learners preferred passive mailing lists over interactive discussion forums and blogs. The paper recommends highlighting the pedagogical purpose of tools offered, giving learners the freedom to choose which tools to use, and conducting further research on sustainability and instructor workload issues in MOOCs. Investigation is also necessary to determine if terms such as course, drop-out, and attrition are appropriate in relation to MOOCs.</p>
<p><a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=2350964"><strong>The MOOC Phenomenon: Who Takes Massive Open Online Courses and Why?</strong></a> (2014) by Gayle Christensen, Andrew Steinmetz, Brandon Alcorn, Amy Bennett, Deirdre Woods, Ezekiel Emanuel<br />
Summary: MOOCs have gained public attention for their potential, but there are no robust, published data that describe who is taking these courses and why. An online survey of students enrolled in at least one of the University of Pennsylvania&#8217;s 32 MOOCs shows that the student population tends to be young, well-educated, and employed, with a majority from developed countries. The main reasons for taking MOOCs are advancing in their current job and satisfying curiosity. Those without access to higher education in developing countries are underrepresented among early adopters.</p>
<p><strong><a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0360131516300793">Exploring the factors affecting MOOC retention: A survey study</a></strong> (2016) by KS Hone, GR El Said<br />
This study examined MOOC retention and completion rates of 379 students at a university in Cairo who were encouraged to take a MOOC of their own choice. Only 32.2% completed an entire course, with no significant differences based on gender, level of study, or MOOC platform. The study found that MOOC Course Content and interaction with the instructor were significant predictors of retention, explaining 79% of the variance.</p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/most-cited-mooc-research/">20 Most Cited Research Papers on MOOCs</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
]]></content:encoded>

<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">What is Digital Art?</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">According to </span><a href="https://www.adobe.com/uk/creativecloud/illustration/discover/digital-art.html#:~:text=Digital%20art%20is%20any%20artwork%20that%20draws%20upon,long%20as%20they%E2%80%99re%20created%2C%20enhanced%20or%20exhibited%20digitally." target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Adobe</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">:</span></p>
<blockquote><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Digital art is any artwork that draws upon digital technology as an essential part of its creative process.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">It encompasses a wide range of techniques, from digital drawings, paintings and illustration, to photos, videos and even sculpture. All can be classed as digital art, so long as they’re created, enhanced or exhibited digitally.</span></p></blockquote>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Some of the different forms of digital art include digital drawing, digital painting, digital sculpting, animation, pixel art, photography, and video. So you can understand that the spectrum of digital art is vast and enables you to explore and choose what you want to work on.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Some of the most popular digital art software include </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-adobe-illustrator-courses-beginners/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Adobe Illustrator</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-adobe-photoshop-courses-beginners/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Adobe Photoshop</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-procreate-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Procreate</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. You’ll get the opportunity to learn more about these applications and how to use them for your digital art in the courses in this guide.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">Why are Digital Art Skills Important?</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Digital art is also backed up by a ton of media outlets for artists on the web, from opportunities to develop content for social media and digital marketing, to animation and game development. This is certainly the perfect moment to start learning and improve your skills, even more considering the global art market was valued at 65.1 billion dollars in 2021, rapidly recovering to pre-pandemic levels.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">There are over 5,000 jobs available for digital artists on </span><a href="https://www.glassdoor.com/Job/digital-artist-jobs-SRCH_KO0,14.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Glassdoor</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, nearly 400 jobs on LinkedIn, and nearly a hundred freelance jobs on </span><a href="https://www.upwork.com/freelance-jobs/digital-art/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Upwork</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Also, the </span><a href="https://www.salary.com/research/salary/posting/digital-artist-salary" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">average salary</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> for a digital artist is $67,020 a year in the United States (as of November 2022).</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What is My Experience with Digital Art?</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">As far as drawing on iPad is concerned, I’ve used apps such as Autodesk Sketchbook and Tayasui Sketches. And on my desktop, I’ve drawn in Photoshop using graphic tablets.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Besides that, I am a </span><a href="https://www.coursera.org/instructor/archisha-bhar" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Guided Project Instructor</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and a Beta Tester at Coursera, having tested many courses before they’re officially launched. I have taken </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/@archisha" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">over 50 online courses</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> in various subjects.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My experience as an online learner and teacher has given me some perspective on what to look for in an online course. I used my experience to evaluate each course in this list.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone wp-image-79247 size-full" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1.png" alt="Find your next course." width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-1-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Course Ranking Methodology</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">I built this ranking following the now tried-and-tested methodology I used in previous rankings (</span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/category/best-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">you can find them all here</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">). It involves a three-step process:</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Research:</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> I started by leveraging Class Central’s database with </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subjects" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">100K online courses</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and 200K+ reviews. Then, I made a preliminary selection of </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subject/digital-art" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">1.5K+ digital art courses</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> by rating, reviews, and bookmarks.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Evaluate:</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> I read through reviews on Class Central, Reddit, and course providers to understand what other learners thought about each course and combined it with my own experience as a </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/@archisha" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">learner</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Select:</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Well-made courses were picked if they presented valuable and engaging content and they have to fit in a set of criteria and be ranked accordingly: comprehensive curriculum, release date, affordability, ratings and enrollments.</span></li>
</ol>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The end result is a unique selection of courses that combines a decade of Class Central data and my own experience as an online learner to try to get the best of both worlds. So far, I’ve spent more than 10 hours building this list, and I’ll continue to update it.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">So without further ado, let’s get to my picks for the best digital art online courses.</span></p>
<h2 id="anchor-1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">1. </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-adobe-photoshop-illustrator-digital-paintin-67565" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Digital Painting Master Class : Beginner to Advanced (Udemy)</span></a></h2>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My first pick for the best digital art online course is </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-adobe-photoshop-illustrator-digital-paintin-67565" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Digital Painting Master Class : Beginner to Advanced</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> on Udemy.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This is the most comprehensive digital art course on this list. Focused on digital painting, you’ll cover everything from illustrating characters, creatures, landscapes and more in </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-adobe-photoshop-courses-beginners/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Adobe Photoshop</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-adobe-illustrator-courses-beginners/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Adobe Illustrator</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Whether you are a beginner or a professional digital artist, you’ll benefit from this course as you learn step by step the fundamentals of the software and work your way up to more advanced digital painting techniques used by professionals.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In this course, you’ll start by becoming familiar with the interfaces of Adobe Photoshop and Adobe Illustrator and mastering the most commonly used tools, work on mini projects that will show you the practical applications of Photoshop in the real world, learn professional techniques for lighting, animation and illustration, and explore more advanced digital painting techniques.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">How You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The course is broken down into 15 sections. Each section involves about 1 to 8 hours of work. Concepts are taught through a combination of videos and readings .</span></p>

<h2 id="anchor-2"><span style="font-weight: 400;">2. </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/youtube-you-can-draw-this-120098" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">You Can Draw This! (Art with Flo)</span></a></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85516" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85516" style="width: 1537px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85516" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-You-Can-Draw-This-Art-with-Flo.png" alt="" width="1537" height="768" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-You-Can-Draw-This-Art-with-Flo.png 1537w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-You-Can-Draw-This-Art-with-Flo-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-You-Can-Draw-This-Art-with-Flo-1024x512.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-You-Can-Draw-This-Art-with-Flo-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1537px) 100vw, 1537px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85516" class="wp-caption-text">Drawing a face in Procreate</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My second pick for the best digital art online course is the </span><b>free course</b> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/youtube-you-can-draw-this-120098" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">You Can Draw This!</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, offered by Art with Flo on YouTube.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This course is ideal for those who prefer a more flexible and creative approach to learning digital art and illustration. In order to be able to take this course, it’s better that you have some experience in using Procreate or similar apps. These tutorials are easy to follow and will take you through all the steps of the drawing and painting process. Each video covers one type of drawing from start to finish such as landscape, graffiti. mandala, 3D text, animals and many more.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In this course, the instructor will guide you through the basic setup and step-by-step process to achieve professional results for each tutorial. You will learn hundreds of styles of digital painting and drawing in this course: from outer space landscapes to cute animals, hamburgers, phone wallpapers, mandalas, and much more.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This course will also provide you with some more abstract concepts to help you create 3D typography, work with geometric shapes, neon signs, condensation art, etc. You can take the tutorials in any order as they teach the concepts independently from start to finish.</span></p>

<h2 id="anchor-8"><span style="font-weight: 400;">8. </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-digital-art-101-from-beginner-to-pro-66691" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Complete Beginner&#8217;s Guide to Digital Art (Udemy)</span></a></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85522" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85522" style="width: 1537px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85522" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/8.-Complete-Beginners-Guide-to-Digital-Art-Udemy.png" alt="" width="1537" height="768" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/8.-Complete-Beginners-Guide-to-Digital-Art-Udemy.png 1537w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/8.-Complete-Beginners-Guide-to-Digital-Art-Udemy-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/8.-Complete-Beginners-Guide-to-Digital-Art-Udemy-1024x512.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/8.-Complete-Beginners-Guide-to-Digital-Art-Udemy-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1537px) 100vw, 1537px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85522" class="wp-caption-text">Drawing using squares and cubes</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My eighth pick for the best digital art online course is </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-digital-art-101-from-beginner-to-pro-66691" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Complete Beginner&#8217;s Guide to Digital Art</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> on Udemy.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This comprehensive, in-depth course is not only about digital art but art in general. You’ll start as a beginner or a hobbyist and work your way up to have the mentality of a professional. You’ll build a solid base in (digital) art so that you can enhance your own work. By the end of this course, you’d have mastered the foundations of digital drawing and illustration and started creating art like a pro.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In this course, you’ll learn the basics of line drawing, make simple shapes, understand the relationships between lines and shapes, use lines and shapes to draw from observation, learn the basics of any digital art software, and understand the fundamentals of digital coloring.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">How You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The course is broken down into 16 sections. Each section involves about 30 minutes to 3.5 hours of work. Concepts are taught through a combination of videos and downloadable resources.</span></p>

<h2 id="anchor-9"><span style="font-weight: 400;">9. </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/skillshare-pixel-art-master-course-beginner-to-expert-freelance-level-for-video-games-part-1-3-beginner-44877" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Pixel Art Master Course &#8211; Beginner to Expert/Freelance level &#8211; for Video games &#8211; PART 1/3 (Beginner) (Skillshare)</span></a></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85525" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85525" style="width: 1537px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85525" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/9.-Pixel-Art-Master-Course-Beginner-to-ExpertFreelance-level-for-Video-games-PART-13-Beginner-Skillshare.png" alt="" width="1537" height="768" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/9.-Pixel-Art-Master-Course-Beginner-to-ExpertFreelance-level-for-Video-games-PART-13-Beginner-Skillshare.png 1537w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/9.-Pixel-Art-Master-Course-Beginner-to-ExpertFreelance-level-for-Video-games-PART-13-Beginner-Skillshare-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/9.-Pixel-Art-Master-Course-Beginner-to-ExpertFreelance-level-for-Video-games-PART-13-Beginner-Skillshare-1024x512.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/9.-Pixel-Art-Master-Course-Beginner-to-ExpertFreelance-level-for-Video-games-PART-13-Beginner-Skillshare-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1537px) 100vw, 1537px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85525" class="wp-caption-text">Mislav Majdandžić, instructor</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My ninth pick for the best digital art online course is </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/skillshare-pixel-art-master-course-beginner-to-expert-freelance-level-for-video-games-part-1-3-beginner-44877" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Pixel Art Master Course &#8211; Beginner to Expert/Freelance level &#8211; for Video games &#8211; PART 1/3 (Beginner)</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> on Skillshare.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This course will teach you all you need to know to get started with your very own pixel art for video games. You’ll start from the very basics and move up to more advanced concepts. The course is divided conveniently into different sections, each dedicated to a single topic such as lines and shapes, color and textures, objects etc. At the end of each section, there’s an exercise so that you can apply what you learned.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">First, you’ll explore which software to use for pixel art, such as Photoshop, Pyxel Edit, Aseprite and Piskel. You’ll be introduced to lines and shapes, and shading and lighting (value and contrast basics, positive and negative space, basic geometric shapes, shading a cube, sphere, cylinder, cone and pyramid, and dithering).</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Next, you’ll move on to colors and textures (hue, saturation, value, color theory, color harmony, color palette, wood texture, metal texture, and applying textures to shapes), create objects (principle of creating objects from simple geometric shapes, creating an orange, potion, book, arrow, sword and gun)</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">After that, you’ll work with tiles (what tiles are, tiling basics, grass tile, dirt tile, water tile and tileset), backgrounds (making a simple image, using colors and shapes to create depth, and add reflection on water surface), and characters (creating 8&#215;8, 16&#215;16 and 32&#215;32 pixel art character).</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Finally, you’ll learn about animation (what animation is, simple grass animation, 8&#215;8, 16&#215;16 and 32&#215;32 character walk, run and attack animations).</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">How You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The course is broken down into 71 lessons. Each lesson involves about 1 to 10 minutes of work. Concepts are taught through a combination of videos, projects and downloadable resources.</span></p>

<h2 id="anchor-10"><span style="font-weight: 400;">10. </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/youtube-digital-painting-55055" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Digital Painting (Proko)</span></a></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85523" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85523" style="width: 1537px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85523" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/10.-Digital-Painting-Proko.png" alt="" width="1537" height="768" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/10.-Digital-Painting-Proko.png 1537w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/10.-Digital-Painting-Proko-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/10.-Digital-Painting-Proko-1024x512.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/10.-Digital-Painting-Proko-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1537px) 100vw, 1537px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85523" class="wp-caption-text">Painting Rudolph, the red-nosed reindeer</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My tenth pick for the best digital art online course is the </span><b>free course</b> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/youtube-digital-painting-55055" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Digital Painting</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, offered by Proko on YouTube.</span></p>

		<title>EMOOCs 2023: Call for Papers [Deadline March 15]</title>
		<link>https://www.classcentral.com/report/emoocs-2023-cfp/</link>
					<comments>https://www.classcentral.com/report/emoocs-2023-cfp/#respond</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Manoel Cortes Mendez]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Tue, 28 Feb 2023 11:00:23 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[News]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Conferences]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://www.classcentral.com/report/?p=84060</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>The EMOOCs conference welcomes submissions on all facets of MOOCs. The deadline is fast approaching.</p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/emoocs-2023-cfp/">EMOOCs 2023: Call for Papers [Deadline March 15]</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/12/emoocs-2023-banner-final.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-84061" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/12/emoocs-2023-banner-final.png" alt="EMOOCs conference 2023 banner" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/12/emoocs-2023-banner-final.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/12/emoocs-2023-banner-final-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/12/emoocs-2023-banner-final-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The eighth edition of </span><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">EMOOCs</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, the European MOOCs stakeholder summer, will take place at the Hasso Plattner Institute (HPI), in </span><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/location/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Potsdam, Germany</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, on June 14–16, 2023.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The conference is dedicated to massive open online courses, from ideation to delivery to evaluation. This edition takes a particular interest in the pandemic’s long-lasting impact on MOOCs — most notably, regarding the role moving forward of online education within traditional education.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In 2021, the event was already set to take place at HPI but had to be moved online due to the pandemic. 2023 will mark the return to an in-person conference, though limited online participation will also be possible.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The </span><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/call-for-papers/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">call for papers</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> has been published. Submissions close on <strong>March 15, 2023</strong>.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Program</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">While the detailed agenda has yet to be determined, the conference will include keynotes, lightning talks, panel discussions, and interactive workshops.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In 2023, the conference sessions will be broken down into five tracks:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/business/"><b>Business</b></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, focusing on MOOCs’ place in the enterprise world — most notably, how they may support workforce training and reskilling, and long-term business sustainability.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/international/"><b>International</b></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, focusing on MOOCs on the global stage, with a particular interest for MOOC projects and initiatives rooted in Latin America, Australia, Africa, and Asia.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/policy/"><b>Policy</b></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, focusing on the political and societal issues surrounding MOOCs, such as how policy design may support MOOC development with a view to benefiting the greater number.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/research-and-experience/"><b>Research &amp; Experience</b></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, focusing on the academic and practitioner perspective on MOOCs regarding topics such as instructional design, best use of technology, and outcome analysis.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/workshops/"><b>Workshops</b></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, focusing on MOOC processes, operations, and know-how, through an interactive, participatory approach.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The conference will also be an opportunity to network. A poster session and social activities will facilitate discussion between participants.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Once released, you’ll be able to find the </span><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/program/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">full conference program here</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Call for Papers</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The conference welcomes submissions on a wide variety of MOOC-related topics. This edition has three focal points:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>The long-lasting impact of the pandemic on online education</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">. COVID prompted a global move to online education. As a result, many people who’d never tried online learning before are now familiar with it. So now seems like a good time for a debrief. What was the impact of the pandemic on MOOCs and vice versa, and now that the pandemic impetus on online education has abated, what should be the role of MOOCs moving forward?</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>The normalization of online education as part of regular education</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Be it through the popularization of blended learning or the multiplication of MOOC-based online degrees over the last decade, the line between traditional education and online education has been getting blurrier. What should we expect next in this progression, and how do we get there?</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>The global cooperation around MOOCs</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">. MOOCs are inherently a global phenomenon that calls for international cooperation. What are some of the promising MOOC projects underway, and how can their development be facilitated through cooperation?</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Papers should be submitted in one of the five tracks, and they may take the form of lightweight proposals, short papers, full research papers, or workshop proposals. The conference welcomes the perspectives of many stakeholders, including educators, researchers, technologists, and decision-makers.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The deadline for submitting a paper is <strong>March 15, 2023</strong>. You can find the </span><a href="https://emoocs.hpi.de/index.php/call-for-papers/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">full call for papers here</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Class Central is a media partner of EMOOCs 2023</span></i></p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/emoocs-2023-cfp/">EMOOCs 2023: Call for Papers [Deadline March 15]</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>

										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85497" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Elm-BCG-Banner.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Elm-BCG-Banner.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Elm-BCG-Banner-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/Elm-BCG-Banner-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>Are you fed up with silly problems such as trying to center an image in a box or reuse visual elements on multiple web pages?</p>
<p>Does your code worry you even when it has been ‘completed’ and pushed to production?</p>
<p>Do you get tired of dealing with the complexity of other web development languages and frameworks?</p>
<p>Then you need to check out Elm.</p>
<p>Elm is a functional programming language for building front-end web applications. It&#8217;s highly expressive and easy to read, and it also has a strong focus on user-interface development, which makes it well-suited for building interactive web applications. Many of the latest functional features such as immutability, stateless functions, anonymous functions, and pattern matching are incorporated into the language. But the best part is Elm’s very own architecture which makes managing data flow between various components a breeze.</p>
<p>Elm is a perfect choice for developers who want to build high-quality, interactive web applications with ease and efficiency, which is why companies such as Microsoft, IBM,  NoRedInk, and Prezi use Elm for their front-end applications.</p>
<p>If you’re interested in learning more, continue reading to find my top picks for the best Elm courses. Click on one to skip to the course details:</p>

<h2>What is Elm?</h2>
<p>Elm is a functional programming language for building front-end web applications, initially designed by Evan Czaplicki in 2012. He found that <a href="https://seas.harvard.edu/news/2015/10/alumni-profile-evan-czaplicki-ab-12" target="_blank" rel="noopener">web development was often difficult, error-prone, and frustrating</a>, and he wanted to create a language that would make it easier to build high-quality, interactive web applications. And thus, Elm was born.</p>
<p>Elm is robust. It’s almost impossible to have runtime errors in Elm thanks to its robust static type system, which ensures that the type of variables must be specified before it can be used (either manually or inferred). Hence, a lot of time and effort is saved when it comes to debugging and testing.</p>
<p>Elm also provides a standardized, novel architecture (Model-View-Update) for organizing code, making data flow management between components easy and eliminating the need to compare and contrast multiple frameworks, allowing developers to focus on the problem at hand.</p>
<p>Elm is lightweight and performant. Elm compiles to a small JavaScript file size, making it ideal for web development, especially for applications with limited resources or slow internet connections. Yet, it is even faster than most popular JavaScript frameworks — even without optimizations. Just look at the following graphs!</p>
<figure id="attachment_85505" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85505" style="width: 740px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85505" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/asset-sizes.png" alt="" width="740" height="500" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/asset-sizes.png 740w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/asset-sizes-300x203.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 740px) 100vw, 740px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85505" class="wp-caption-text">from <a href="https://elm-lang.org/news/small-assets-without-the-headache" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Small Assets without the Headache</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure id="attachment_85506" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85506" style="width: 800px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85506" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/everyone.png" alt="" width="800" height="500" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/everyone.png 800w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/everyone-300x188.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/everyone-768x480.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85506" class="wp-caption-text">from <a href="https://elm-lang.org/news/blazing-fast-html-round-two" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Blazing Fast HTML</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Elm is maintainable. Elm, as a functional language, comes with features you’d expect such as immutability, stateless functions, anonymous functions, and pattern matching, that reduces the complexity of code (such as states). Elm can also easily interoperate with existing JavaScript code, so you don’t have to rewrite everything in Elm (yet).</p>
<p>Elm is simple. Although its syntax is inspired by the Meta Language family of languages (like <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-free-haskell-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Haskell</a> and <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/best-ocaml-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">OCaml</a>), which are known for their steep learning curve, Elm instead opts for a simpler yet expressive syntax. Hence, Elm is not only easy-to-learn, but it is also easy-to-reason.</p>
<p>If Elm is so great, <a href="https://github.com/jah2488/elm-companies" target="_blank" rel="noopener">who is using it</a>? Some of the biggest examples include:</p>
<ul>
<li aria-level="1"><a href="https://www.noredink.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">NoRedInk</a>: A popular online marketplace website for language learning, which was one of the first large-scale Elm applications (Evan Czaplicki currently works here).</li>
<li aria-level="1"><a href="https://prezi.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Prezi</a>: A cloud-based presentation software and storytelling tool that uses Elm for the development of their web-based editor (Evan Czaplicki started on Elm here).</li>
<li aria-level="1"><a href="http://brilliant.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Brilliant</a>: An educational website that offers interactive math and science courses for students and professionals. Most of Brilliant’s interactives as well as the <a href="https://youtu.be/gT9Xu-ctNqI" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Diagrammar</a> tool is built in Elm.</li>
<li aria-level="1"><a href="https://www.emirates.com/my/english/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Emirates</a>: The national airline of the United Arab Emirates.</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone wp-image-79248 size-full" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2.png" alt="Find your next course." width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<h2>Best Courses Guides Methodology</h2>
<p>I built this ranking following the now tried-and-tested methodology used in previous Best Courses Guides (<a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/category/best-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">you can find them all here</a>). It involves a three-step process:</p>
<ol>
<li aria-level="1"><b>Research:</b> I started by leveraging Class Central’s database with <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subjects" target="_blank" rel="noopener">100K online courses</a> and 200K+ reviews. Then, I made a preliminary selection of <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subject/elm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Elm courses</a> by rating, reviews, and bookmarks.</li>
<li aria-level="1"><b>Evaluate:</b> I read through reviews on Class Central, Reddit, and course providers to understand what other learners thought about each course and combined it with my own experience as a <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/@Elham" target="_blank" rel="noopener">learner</a>.</li>
<li aria-level="1"><b>Select:</b> Well-made courses were picked if they presented valuable and engaging content and they have to fit in a set of criteria and be ranked accordingly: comprehensive curriculum, affordability, release date, ratings and enrollments.</li>
</ol>

<h2 id="anchor-1">1. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/independent-a-gentle-introduction-to-elm-programming-language-122049" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Beginning Elm: a gentle introduction to Elm programming language (Pawan Poudel)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85498" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-Beginning-Elm_-a-gentle-introduction-to-Elm-programming-language-Pawan-Poudel.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-Beginning-Elm_-a-gentle-introduction-to-Elm-programming-language-Pawan-Poudel.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-Beginning-Elm_-a-gentle-introduction-to-Elm-programming-language-Pawan-Poudel-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/1.-Beginning-Elm_-a-gentle-introduction-to-Elm-programming-language-Pawan-Poudel-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>My #1 pick for the best Elm course is <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/independent-a-gentle-introduction-to-elm-programming-language-122049" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Beginning Elm</a> authored by Pawan Poudel.</p>
<p>This <b>free</b> online book is a gentle introduction to the Elm programming language. I chose this as my top pick as it is full of bite-sized nuggets of information. You’ll learn the basic syntax and semantics of Elm and gradually shift towards building interactive modern web applications, picking up the best design principles and patterns that can be applied to every programming language out there.</p>
<p>You should have a basic understanding of programming to take this course, as well as a solid foundation in HTML/CSS.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>The course begins with a brief introduction to Elm programming where you’ll install the Elm Platform and explore the various high-level tools and concepts needed to build a simple web-page, such as the Elm programming language, architecture, compiler, and runtime.</p>
<p>One of the hardest things about learning a programming language is getting accustomed to its syntax. You’ll learn the basic syntax as well as data structures like lists, arrays, and records which you can use complex mattern-patching code for nested logic. You’ll also learn how to import third-party modules from elsewhere. Everything you’ve learned so far will help you appreciate and understand how Elm’s immutable values, pure functions, and a powerful type system lead to reliable and maintainable programs.</p>
<p>Elm is both a programming language and an architecture. Both are needed to build robust front-end web applications. After studying the programming language, you’ll study how the Elm architecture manages data flow in apps using the Model View Update pattern. By learning how to create, read, update, and delete data from a server by sending HTTP requests, you’ll be able to build single-page applications that can interact with JavaScript using ports, flags, and custom elements.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course consists of 8 chapters in total. You’ll learn by reading through the course chapters, looking at the example code, and implementing what you’ve learned on your PC.</p>

<h2 id="anchor-2">2. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/frontend-masters-introduction-to-elm-v2-118048" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Introduction to Elm, v2 (Frontend Masters)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85499" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Elm-v2-Frontend-Masters.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Elm-v2-Frontend-Masters.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Elm-v2-Frontend-Masters-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/2.-Introduction-to-Elm-v2-Frontend-Masters-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>My #2 pick for the best Elm course is <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/frontend-masters-introduction-to-elm-v2-118048" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Introduction to Elm, v2</a> on Frontend Masters by the legendary Richard Feldman.</p>
<p>Who is he? He’s well known in the Elm community as the author of ‘<a href="https://www.manning.com/books/elm-in-action" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Elm in Action</a>’, a thoroughly comprehensive book on Elm. He also worked for NoRedInk, one of the largest companies using Elm in production, and is currently working on making a revolutionary programming language heavily inspired by Elm called ‘<a href="https://www.roc-lang.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Roc</a>’.</p>
<p>In this <b>paid</b> course with <b>5 courses</b> <b>free trial</b>, Richard will guide you through the basics of the Elm programming language by building a complete Elm application. This application, a Medium clone, is called Conduit (get it? Haha). You’ll utilize elm-package for access to the Elm package ecosystem, incorporate elm-test for writing tests, work with third-party JavaScript libraries through JavaScript Interop, and more!</p>
<p>You should have some knowledge of JavaScript prior to taking this course.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll build a Medium clone called Conduit. You’ll start by setting up the basic Elm template for the project and learn Elm renders a page using the virtual DOM. Then, you’ll learn some of Elm’s basic syntax such as variables, booleans, if statements, and strings. Elm’s functional programming aspects will also be discussed, like how functions work, why data structures such as lists and records are immutable, and how to manipulate the DOM in spite of immutability.</p>
<p>The Elm architecture is the not-so-secret ingredient that makes Elm great. You’ll study how to make applications interactive using the Elm architecture. Afterward, you’ll explore Elm’s type system, including type annotations, the Maybe type, and making your own custom types.</p>
<p>The next section of the course goes further into web development. You’ll learn how to decode JSON structures and then talk to servers using HTTP requests. Finally, you’ll see how to interoperate with existing JavaScript code using Elm subscriptions.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course has 5–6 hours worth of material consisting of nine lessons and nine exercises.</p>

<li aria-level="1">Richard is the author of <a href="https://www.manning.com/books/elm-in-action" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Elm in Action</a>.  He’s written a lot of JavaScript, dating back to the pre-jQuery days, but since 2015 has spent more time writing Elm and Rust. Over the years he’s created several popular Elm packages, including elm-css, elm-test, and elm-json-decode-pipeline; he’s also created the JavaScript seamless-immutable library and a fully-featured programming language compiler in Rust. He hosts both the Philadelphia Elm Meetup and the Philadelphia Rust Meetup.</li>
<li aria-level="1">I really liked this talk of his called <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vzfy4EKwG_Y" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Outperforming Imperative with Pure Functional Languages</a> where he discusses how he managed to make Roc blazingly fast. Check it out if you want to know more about the internals of languages.</li>
</ul>

<h2 id="anchor-3">3. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-elm-the-complete-guide-122046" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Elm &#8211; The Complete Guide (Carlos Saltos)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85500" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Elm-The-Complete-Guide-Carlos-Saltos.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Elm-The-Complete-Guide-Carlos-Saltos.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Elm-The-Complete-Guide-Carlos-Saltos-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/02/3.-Elm-The-Complete-Guide-Carlos-Saltos-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p>My #3 pick for the best Elm course is <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-elm-the-complete-guide-122046" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Elm &#8211; The Complete Guide</a>, which teaches you how to build modern web apps using Elm. This comprehensive <b>paid </b>course will teach you through hands-on learning, where you’ll create several websites to help you master the language, architecture, and design principles.</p>
<p>To take this course, you should know HTML. No JavaScript experience is required.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll quickly get started learning the language by building a “Hello, World!” Elm program from the ground up. This serves as your first introduction to the Elm Live development cycle, where you’ll write code and see changes quickly reflect itself in your program in real-time.</p>
<p>Afterward, you’ll embark on many different web development projects to help you grasp the principles of the Elm Architecture. Some of these projects include learning how to create visually appealing yet accessible user interfaces that can adapt to different screen sizes with Elm UI, presenting data in a clear and concise way with Elm Chart, and creating animations using SVG and Elm VG. You’ll also learn how to make API calls and handle JSON data with Elm JSON, and debug web applications by traveling back in time with the Elm Debugger. Finally, you’ll optimize and deploy your web application to production using JAMStack or other options such as DigitalOcean, AWS, and Nginx.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course is 21–22 hours long. You’ll learn by watching the series of hands-on videos, where you’ll follow along with the instructor to create beautiful websites as projects.</p>
